Summary 146:
Statistics on health status and health determinants — European statistical system
Statistics on healthcare status and healthcare determinants – European statistical systems
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1350/2007/EC on the production and dissemination of Community statistics
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that the European Union (EU) has comparable and comparable statistics on health and social determinants (HSDs) for all EU countries.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to the statistics on HSDs that are based on self-assessment and compiled from population surveys such as the European Health Interview Survey (EHIS), as well as other statistics compiled from administrative sources such as those on morbidity or accidents and injuries at work.
It does not apply to statistics on the health status of EU citizens.
The statistics covered by the regulation are:
statistical indicators, such as structural indicators, sustainable development indicators and European Community Health Indicators (ECHI),
the other sets of indicators which it is necessary to develop for the purpose of monitoring Community actions in the fields of public health and health and safety at work;
health determinants, which are defined in the European Social Fund’s (ESF) Statistical Code of Practice (see summary);
statistics on health care and long-term care.
National and EU statistical authorities
The European Commission is responsible for the production, dissemination and management of the statistics. The Commission is assisted by Eurostat, the European statistics office and the European Commission Statistics Directorate-General principles
The Commission has the power to adopt implementing measures for the implementation of the regulation.
EU countries must ensure that:
the national and EU statistics authorities:
collect comparable data and information;
provide the relevant information to the Commission and Eurostat;
ensure that the national statistics authorities have the necessary resources to carry out their tasks;
use the statistical methods and procedures for collecting and disseminating the data;
have the necessary technical resources to ensure the quality of the data they collect and the availability of the information they provide;
organise the collection of the statistical data and the dissemination of the results of their analyses;
inform the Commission, Eurostat and the EU countries of the methods and methods used to collect and disseminate the statistics they collect.
Data protection
The EU data protection supervisor has been consulted by the Commission.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
    данскага барка гарша  года  
It has applied since 1 January 2008.
BACKGROUND
 
  изнанна ванка, гострака and гъланца are the main sources of data on health in the EU.
For more information, see:
Health statistics (European Commission).

Summary 147:
Data on job vacancies
Data on jobs vacancies
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2006 on job vacancy statistics
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down minimum requirements for EU countries to provide the European Commission and the European Central Bank (ECB) with reliable, comparable and up-to-date quarterly data on the number of jobs available in the European Union (EU).
It aims to ensure that EU countries provide the Commission with reliable and comparable information on the availability of job vacancies.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all economic activities defined by the common classification system for economic activities in the EU (NACE) in force, except for households as employers and the activities of extraterritorial organisations and bodies.
EU countries must provide the data using business surveys. The sources of all data provided must be specified.
The Commission (Eurostat) determines the reference dates, formats and deadlines for the collection of the data.
National sample schemes may be established and coordinated by the Commission to produce Community estimates where national sample schemes do not meet the EU requirements with regard to quarterly data collection.
Data transmitted by EU countries must be sent to the Commission by the end of the third quarter of each calendar year. The date of the first reference quarter must also be determined in accordance with the regulatory procedure with scrutiny referred to in Article 9(2) of the regulation.
Each EU country must send the Commission a report every 3 years on the quality of data transmitted.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULTRY?
The EU countries had to incorporate this regulation into national law by 31 December 2006.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has been responsible for implementing the EU’s employment strategy for the period 2007-2013.
For more information, see:
‘Job vacancies’ on the Commission's website.

Summary 148:
Hybrid fuel — type-approval of hydrogen systems and components
Hybrid fuels — type ofapproval
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2008 on type approval of hydrogen-powered vehicles
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the requirements for the type approval and technical specifications for the installation of hydrogen propulsion systems and their components in motor vehicles.
It lays down the test procedures for hydrogen containers designed to use compressed (gaseous) hydrogen.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
hydrogen systems, components and systems intended to be installed in vehicles for the use of hydrogen (e.g. hydrogen containers);
vehicle interface systems;
overpressure protection systems; and
heat exchanger failure detection systems.
Manufacturers must ensure that their products comply with the requirements of the regulation and the technical specifications laid down by implementing measures adopted by the European Commission.
National authorities must grant EU type approval to manufacturers if they consider that they have carried out the necessary tests to ensure that the systems and systems comply with this regulation.
The manufacturer must keep the results of the tests throughout the service life of the vehicle and notify the competent authorities of the results.
EU countries may refuse to grant type approval if they believe that a system or system does not meet the requirements set out in the regulation or if it does not comply with its technical specifications.
Importers must carry out the required tests to prove that the hydrogen system or component complies with the regulation’s requirements.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLACE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
 
   
The legislation entered into force on 24 February 2008.
BACKGROUND
The European Union (EU) has a comprehensive system for type approval for motor vehicles for hydrogen propulsion.
For more information, see:
‘Hybrid vehicles’ on the European Agency for Safety and Health at Work website
* KEY TERMS
* Hydrogen propulsion system: a system that uses compressed hydrogen for the propulsion of a motor vehicle.
* Container: a container designed to contain compressed hydrogen that is filled with compressed hydrogen to provide hydrogen to a vehicle for use as a fuel.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 			
Commission Regulation (EC), Euratom, Euratom of 24 January 2008 on type-authorisation of hydrogen powered vehicles

Summary 150:
Legal cooperation between EU countries and non-EU countries on specific civil justice issues
Lawful cooperation within the European Union (EU)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1049/2001 on agreements with third countries on certain civil justice matters
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a procedure for EU countries wishing to conclude legal cooperation with non-european countries to do so.
It aims to ensure that an agreement envisaged by an EU country does not render EU law ineffective and does not undermine the proper functioning of the system established by that law, or undermine the EU’s external relations policy.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to legal cooperation in civil matters between the EU countries.
Amendments to existing agreements
An amendment to an existing agreement may be made only if it regulates in substance the same specific legal issues.
The amendment must be accompanied by a copy of the existing agreement, the draft agreement or the draft proposal, and any other relevant documentation.
Authorisation to conclude the agreement
The EU country concerned must notify the European Commission of its intentions to open or continue formal negotiations on an agreement as well as to conclude an agreement.
Notification must be given by letter or by electronic means.
If the envisaged agreement meets the conditions set out in Article 4(2), the Commission must, within 90 days of receipt of the notification, give a reasoned decision on the application of the EU country authorising it to open formal negotiations.
Refusal to authorise the opening of negotiations
An EU country may, within 30 days of receiving the decision, refuse to enter into discussions with the Commission. The Commission must then submit a report to the European Parliament and to the Council on the reasons for its refusal.
Public access to documents
The Commission must ensure that any information identified as confidential is treated in accordance with the public access to European Parliament, Council and Commission documents.

Summary 151:
Statistics on migration and asylum
Statistics on migrants and refugees
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2008 — common rules for the collection and compilation of Community statistics on migration
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for EU countries to provide the European Commission (Eurostat) with statistics on the number of migrants and asylum seekers in the European Union (EU).
It aims to improve the completeness and degree of harmonisation of these statistics.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to the EU countries’ statistics on:
the number of residence permits issued to persons who are third-country nationals, disaggregated as follows:
permits issued during the reference period whereby the person is being granted permission to reside for a period of 3 months;
temporary visas issued for the duration of a visa or immigration status;
visas granted to non-EU nationals who are granted temporary visas for the period of their stay in the EU.
EU countries must provide Eurostat with the following statistics:
total number of persons illegally entering the EU and staying illegally;
the total number of people who are illegally resident in EU countries;
number of persons who have entered the EU illegally and who are staying illegally.
The data must be collected within 3 months of the end of the reference year.
Data sources and quality standards
Eurostat must ensure that the data sources used are up-to-date and that they meet the standards of impartiality, reliability, objectivity, scientific independence, cost-effectiveness, confidentiality and statistical confidentiality.
National authorities must ensure the quality of the data they collect is maintained and that the information they provide conforms with the standards set out in the regulation’s annexes and annexes.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGUMENT APPLYORK?
    даранска года  городна баркова водскога  
It entered into force on 1 January 2008.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission is responsible for collecting and compiling EU statistics for the purposes of monitoring the development and implementation of EU legislation and policy.
For more information, see:
EU statistics (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Migration: the movement of people, goods and capital across borders of the EU, including flows from one EU country to that of another.
* Asylum seeker: a person who is seeking asylum in another EU country and who has been granted asylum in that country.

Summary 153:
Conservation of marine biological resources in the Mediterranean and Black Sea (CFP)
Conservation and management of Marine Biological Resources in the Middle East and North Africa (CFCN)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2010 on the conservation of marine Biological Resources and the management of fisheries targeting them
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that the European Union (EU) fisheries policy is compatible with the Convention on Biological Diversity (CBD) and the United Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea (UNCLOS).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The CFP is the legal framework for the conservation, management and sustainable use of the marine resources of the Mediterranean, Black Sea and North African seas.
It applies to:
fisheries targeting fish stocks and fishery products;
fishing opportunities allocated to EU countries for each fish stock or fishery;
the management of the fisheries targeting these stocks and fisheries by EU countries.
EU fisheries policy
EU countries are responsible for:
collecting biological, environmental, technical, and socio-economic data necessary for fisheries management, managing those data and making them available to end–users, including bodies designated by the Commission.
Managing fisheries
The EU fisheries policy must be based on the best available scientific advice.
In close cooperation with the Commission, EU countries must coordinate their data collection activities with other EU countries in the same region, and make every effort to coordinate their actions with non-EU countries having sovereignty or jurisdiction over the same waters.
Monitoring
The European Commission is responsible for monitoring and monitoring the fisheries policy of EU countries and the fisheries management of non–EU countries. The Commission must adopt the measures, taking into account any scientific advice, within 3 months from receipt of a complete request.
Fisheries management
The Commission must:
monitor and monitor the fishing activities of EU fisheries operators;
assess the impact of non-compliance with the CFP on the fishery and the marine environment;
make recommendations to the EU countries on the future management of their fisheries;
take appropriate action to ensure the sustainable management of fishery resources;
ensure that EU countries’ fishing capacity does not exceed 10 % of the permitted landings;
provide the Commission with information on the number of vessels fishing in EU waters;
implement measures to prevent or reduce illegal fishing.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
Directive 2010/552/EC has applied since 25 March 2010 and had to become law in the EU Member States by 25 March 2011.
Directives 2014/11/EU and 2015/13/EU have applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
    *

‘The Mediterranean’ on the European Commission’s website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 
  бодска барка  гарша

Summary 154:
The common organisation of the markets in fishery and aquaculture products (CMO)
The common operation of the fisheries markets in the EU
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1380/2013 on the common market for fishery products
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to establish a common framework for the management of the European fisheries markets.
KEY POINTS
The regulation sets out the objectives of the CMO, which are to:
foster market stability and a closer correlation between supply and demand;
encourage the appropriate and representative participation of small-scale producers;
improve the transparency of fishery production and marketing plans;
ensure that producer organisations and inter-branch organisations are recognised by the European Commission;
provide information to consumers on the fishery markets in EU countries.
The CMO is governed by a set of rules and implementing acts.
It is managed by the Commission, which has the power to adopt implementing acts concerning:
the format and structure of the producer organisations’ production plans,
the procedure and time-limits for the submission by producers organisations and the approval by EU countries of the production plans referred to in Article 28 of the regulation;
compliance with common marketing standards;
market intelligence;
recognition of producer organisations;
the establishment of associations of producers organisations.

Summary 155:
Securities settlement systems (SDS)
SDSS
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 648/2012 on the establishment of securities settlement systems
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the establishment, operation and supervision of the European Securities and Markets Authority (ESMA), the European Union’s competent national authority for the regulation of the securities settlement system (CSD).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to the establishment and operation of securities settlements systems (CSDs) in the EU.
It does not apply to the operation of depositary institutions (DIs).
It applies to all financial institutions, including banks, insurance companies, pension funds and other financial institutions.
Settlement procedures
The CSD must be authorised by the competent national authorities of the EU country in which it is established.
The competent authorities have the power to:
grant or refuse to grant authorisation to a CSD if they consider that it poses a risk to the stability of the financial system of the host EU country;
suspend or restrict the activities of the CSD in the event that it fails to comply with the requirements laid down in the regulation;
impose administrative peciary sanctions if it does not comply with these sanctions;
ensure the orderly winding-down or restructuring of its operations and services if it is unable to raise sufficient capital to meet the requirements;
provide services that contribute to enhancing the safety, efficiency and transparency of the markets and that do not create undue risks to their core services;
establish an interoperable link between CSDs in the host country and the other EU countries;
require the competent authorities to cooperate with each other in order to ensure the orderly operation of the system.
Authorisation
An EU country must designate one competent authority to be responsible for cooperation with other countries’ competent CSDs established in its territory and must inform ESMA of any such cooperation.
Cooperation between authorities
EU countries must designate a single competent authority responsible for coordinating the cooperation between their competent authorities.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLAW APPLY?
    и  ба  бараковскодна бодска габов года  фонск городка
It has applied since 18 June 2012 and had to become law in the Member States by 18 June 2015.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a number of measures to improve the functioning of EU-wide securities markets.
For more information, see:
‘Settlement systems’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Depositary institution: a financial institution that holds securities on behalf of a client.

Cohesion Fund for transport infrastructure — environmental and trans-European transport infrastructure (Cohesion funds)
Cohesion fund for transportation infrastructure — environment and trans - European transport infrastructure
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1315/2013 establishing the European Regional Development Fund for Transport infrastructure
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes the European regional development fund (ERDF) to provide financial support to projects in the fields of environment and transport infrastructure in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The Cohesion Fund is the EU’s main investment instrument for the development of transport infrastructure.
It provides financial support for projects in areas such as:
transport infrastructure;
environmental and energy;
infrastructure for sustainable development and energy.
The European Commission is responsible for setting out the investment priorities for the ERDF and the Cohesion fund. These investment priorities are set out in the framework of the European Investment Bank (EIB).
The objectives of the EIB are:
investment in the environment, including areas related to sustainable development, energy and energy which present environmental benefits;
transportation infrastructure, including infrastructure for the transport of goods, services and capital;
enhancing institutional capacity of public authorities and stakeholders and efficient public administration through actions to strengthen the institutional capacity and the efficiency of public administrations and public services related to the implementation of the investment objectives;
technical assistance.
In order to ensure that projects are prioritised according to their environmental and energy needs, the European Commission sets out common output indicators (i.e. output indicators) for each investment priority.
These indicators must be expressed in quantitative or qualitative terms.

Summary 157:
The European Regional Development Fund (ERDF) — financial support for the least developed regions of the European Union (EU)
The European regional development fund (ERGDF) is a financial instrument designed to support the development of regions in the EU which suffer from severe and permanent natural or demographic handicaps such as the northernmost regions with very low population density and island, cross-border and mountain regions.
ACT
Regulation (EC) No 552/2013 of the Council of the EU of 21 December 2013 establishing the European Regional development Fund (the ERDF)
SUMMARY
WHAT DOES THIS REGULATION DO?
The ERDF provides financial support to regions which are most deprived of resources and have the least development potential.
The aim of the ERDF is to contribute to reducing disparities between the levels of development of the various regions and to reducing the backwardness of the least favoured regions, among which particular attention is to be paid to regions that suffer from:
the most deprived regions of Europe (i.e. those with a population of less than 500,000),
the least developed countries (i).
KEY POINTS
Scope of support
The EU’s investment for growth and jobs goal (IGJ goal) is the main objective of this ERDF. It aims to increase investment in the creation of jobs and growth in the labour market by investing in infrastructure, particularly in the transport sector, in order to improve the quality of life of people and improve the competitiveness of the economy.
It also aims to support innovative actions in the area of sustainable urban development.
Objectives
The main objectives of the investment goal are to:
increase investment in infrastructure;
support growth and job creation by:
increasing the productivity of workers and entrepreneurs;
improving the efficiency of businesses;
encouraging investment in research and innovation;
promoting the sustainable use of natural resources;
ensuring the sustainability of the environment;
developing sustainable urban areas;
reducing the risk of climate change;
contributing to the sustainable management of energy resources.
Programme objectives
The investment goals are set out in the common output indicators (CEI) and the programme-specific result indicators (PSI).
The common outputs are expressed in quantitative or qualitative terms. The CEI and PSI indicators are set for 2023 and 2023 respectively. The ERDF contributes to achieving the CEI targets by providing financial support in the form of:
investment in infrastructure (airport infrastructure);
research and innovation (research and technological development);
economic development (e.g. urban development).
In addition, the European Commission has the power to adopt delegated acts, delegated by the European Parliament and the Council, to authorise the allocation of resources to the different categories of investment goals.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULATIONS APPLY?
Directive 2013/52/EC entered into force on 1 January 2014.

Summary 158:
European Regional Development Fund (ERDF) — European territorial cooperation goal
European regional development fund (ERGDF) – European regional development goal
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2017/852 — European Regional Development Framework
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
    барганскакованна грандана  годанца бездарскога вастанка  формальна — European Region Development Fund
It sets out the EU’s European territorial development goal for the period 2014-2020.
It aims to reduce disparities between the levels of development of the various regions and to reduce the backwardness of the least favoured regions, among which particular attention is to be paid to rural areas, areas affected by industrial transition, and regions which suffer from severe and permanent natural or demographic handicaps such as the northernmost regions with very low population density and island, cross-border and mountain regions.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries and the European Social Fund (ESF) and the Cohesion Fund for the 2014-20 programming period and to the EU countries’ Member States.
The ERDF is designed to contribute to reducing disparities between regions by:
improving the quality of life in the least developed regions;
increasing social inclusion, combating poverty and any discrimination;
encouraging regional integration;
promoting regional cohesion;
supporting regional development in the most deprived regions of the European Union (EU).
Programmes
The EU countries must designate the managing authorities responsible for managing the ERDF and the managing authority of the relevant cooperation programme. The managing authorities are responsible for:
designating beneficiaries;
setting priorities;
monitoring and evaluation;
providing technical assistance;
assessing the effectiveness of the programme;
drawing up a common output indicator for each programme.
Funding
The funding is divided into 3 categories:
cross-border cooperation,
interregional cooperation and
transnational cooperation.
Programme objectives
The programme objectives are expressed in quantitative or qualitative terms. They are set out in the annex to the regulation.
They include:
the objective of promoting social inclusion and combating poverty;
the thematic objectives of promoting regional integration and regional cohesion, including through actions to promote social and economic stability in the regions concerned, in particular through action to promote cohesion between communities.
In addition, the programme objectives may also include the objectives of:
support for regional development and regional integration in the fields of education, health and social protection;
investment for growth and jobs;
research and innovation;
transport;
education and training;
economic development;
environmental and social policy;
health and safety;
employment and social inclusion;
regional development and social cohesion; and
economic and social development.
Coordination
The managing authorities must:
coordinate the co-ordination of ERDF support for each of the 3 categories of programmes;
set up a monitoring and evaluation mechanism;
ensure that the programme is implemented in line with the objectives set out by the European Commission;
establish a coordination mechanism for the management of the programmes.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 1 January 2018.
BACKGROUND
 
  Баркоднангрфаникан гардалкаговка has been amended several times, most recently in 2017.
For more information, see:
‘European Region Development Framework’ on the European External Action Service's website.

Summary 159:
Smart grids: smart energy infrastructure
Smart energy infrastructure: smart electricity infrastructure
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2013 on smart grids
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the smart grid* and energy storage* sectors of the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to projects of common interest (i.e. projects that are likely to have a significant impact on the EU’s energy security, energy efficiency and supply security) in the electricity and gas sectors.
It does not apply to projects which are not part of the electricity or gas sectors, but which are part of those sectors and which have the potential to have significant impacts on the energy security of the EU.
Decision No 1364/2006/EC was repealed by Regulation (EU) 2018/852 on the smart grids directive.
The European Commission is responsible for the implementation of the regulation.
Implementation
The Commission must ensure that the regulation is implemented in a transparent and transparent manner.
Regulatory authorities must ensure a stable and predictable regulatory framework with incentives for smart grids, including long-term incentives, that are commensurate with the level of specific risk of the project.
National authorities must:
ensure that smart grids comply with the technical specifications set out by the European Network of Transmission System Operators (ENTSO) for electricity and the European Gas Transmission System Operator (EGTSO for Gas) by 16 May 2015;
provide the European Commission with a manual of procedures for the permit granting process applicable to smart grids;
implement a system wide cost-benefit analysis of smart grids.
Transparency and public participation
The competent national authority must publish a manual on the procedure for granting permits for smart grid projects.
EU countries must ensure the transparency and participation of the public in the decision-making process.
In addition, the Commission must provide the European Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee and the Committee of the Regions with a report on the application of the legislation.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
It entered into force on 16 May 2013.

Summary 160:
Out-of-court dispute resolution (ODR) for online sales and service contracts (ODRs)
Out of court dispute resolution(ODRs) — online sales or service contracts
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2017/852 — out-of court dispute redress for online sellers and service providers
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to provide consumers with a single point of entry to resolve disputes with online sellers or service providers.
KEY POINTS
Directive 2013/11/EU sets out the rules for the out of court resolution of disputes between consumers and traders.
The regulation applies to online sales* and service* contracts.
It does not apply to disputes between traders and consumers where the consumer is habitually resident in the EU country where the contract is concluded.
EU countries must ensure that consumers have the right to access the judicial system in the event of a dispute over an online sale or service contract.
In addition, EU countries must set up a dispute resolution system (DRS).
The ODR platform provides consumers with an online dispute resolution tool. It allows them to lodge a complaint against an online seller or service provider and to have the dispute resolved by an ADR (advisory and dispute resolution) entity.
Disputes can be resolved by either the consumer or the ADR entity, if:
the consumer has not been able to prove that the seller or the service provider is liable;
the trader has not complied with the conditions of the contract; or
the dispute has been resolved by the trader or the trader’s intermediary by means of the ODR.
An ODR can be set up in any EU country, provided that the consumer has the right of access to judicial proceedings in that EU country.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
    дарганска гаранка  годанца  
It has applied since 20 May 2017.
BACKGROUND
 
Directives 2013/12/EU and 2013/13/EU introduce measures to improve consumer protection in the online market.
For more information, see:
Online sales and services (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Online sale and service contract: a contract where a seller or a service provider offers goods or services to a consumer through a website or by other electronic means.
* Service contract: an agreement to provide a service for a consumer to perform a service or perform a task for the consumer.
ACT

Summary 161:
The European Union’s (EU) common agricultural policy (CAP) — the basic and area-based payments for farmers
the European Union's common agriculture policy for farmers — the basis for the European Union Agricultural Fund (EUAFRIC)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 561/2013 on the basic payment scheme
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the basic payments system for farmers in the EU.
It aims to ensure that EU countries’ governments provide the same level of financial support to farmers across the EU, irrespective of whether they are natural or legal persons.
KEY POINTS
Direct payments
The basic payment system is based on a fixed percentage of the gross national product (GNP) for each EU country.
The level of support is calculated by dividing the national or regional ceiling for the basic scheme by the total number of young farmers applying for direct payments for the year 2014.
Each EU country decides how much it will grant to each farmer for each hectare of land under the basic system for the 2014-2020 period.
In order to promote the sustainable development of agriculture in areas with specific natural constraints, EU countries are able to use part of their direct payments ceilings to grant an annual area based payment to all farmers operating in those areas or in some of those areas, where decided by the EU country, where they decide by an EU country or region.
Annex I of the regulation sets out how much each country will grant each farmer in each of the following areas:
the basic payment for 2014 and for the following years:
a minimum of €1.
a maximum of €2.
the annual national ceiling set out in Annex II.
an annual maximum amount of €3.5 million for each country for each year for the period 2015-2020.
A maximum amount for each region of the EU is set by the European Commission.
National authorities must notify the European Parliament and the Council of the total value of all the entitlements, including special entitlements for 2014-2022.
EU countries must also notify the Commission of the number of hectares covered by the special agricultural entitlements and the total amount of support allocated for rural development.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
The regulation has applied since 1 January 2013.
BACKGROUND
Directive 2014/561/Euratom is part of the European Agricultural Fund for Rural Development (EURAFRIC).
For more information, see:
‘The European Agriculture Fund’ (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENT

Summary 162:
Support programme for the smaller Aegean islands (Aegean Regional Development Fund) (2007-2013)
Support programme provisionally granted by the European Union (EU) to Greece for the development of the smaller islands
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 376/2008 of the European Parliament and of the Council establishing a support programme for Greece
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to provide financial support to the small islands of the eastern Mediterranean region in order to encourage them to develop their agricultural production.
It sets out the rules for the operation of the support programme.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all the islands in the eastern and central Mediterranean region, except the islands of Crete and Evia, which are part of the western Mediterranean region.
Objectives
The objectives of the programme are to:
promote the sustainable development of small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs) in the area of agricultural production;
support the development and sustainable use of natural resources in the region;
improve the quality of agricultural products;
encourage the use of sustainable methods of transport and storage;
increase the productivity of the local agricultural sector;
provide technical assistance to the local authorities;
facilitate trade in agricultural products between the EU and the islands.
The support programme consists of a number of measures, including:
support for the marketing and transport of raw and processed products outside the EU;
supply of local agricultural products to the islands;
protection of the environment;
promotion of tourism;
exchange of information on the activities of the SMEs;
monitoring of the implementation of the aid.
Implementation
The programme is implemented by means of the measures referred to in Chapters III, IV and V. Each measure may include a variety of actions.
Measures to promote small and mid-sized businesses
The European Commission adopts implementing acts establishing the requirements in accordance with which products covered by the specific supply arrangements may be exported to non-EU countries or dispatched to the rest of the EU.
EU countries may submit to the Commission duly substantiated proposals for amendments to those measures within the context of the financial allocation to bring them more into line with the requirements of smaller islands and the strategy proposed. These amendments must be approved by the Commission within 3 months of the submission of the proposal.
Regulatory measures to protect the environment
The Commission must ensure that:
the measures adopted by the EU countries are compatible with the EU’s environmental legislation;
the EU countries’ environmental legislation is compatible with those of the other EU countries; and
the European Commission has adopted implementing acts to ensure that the measures are applied in a uniform manner and that the advantage has in fact been passed on up to the end-user.
In addition, the Commission must establish a register of operators and a system of certificates, based on the certificates referred to above, to ensure the proper functioning of the scheme.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
It entered into force on 1 January 2009.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘The smaller islands’ on the European Commission's website.

Summary 163:
Road transport statistics: collection and transmission of data during the first quarter of the survey period (1999-2007)
Road transport Statistics: collection, transmission and dissemination
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/1999 on the collection and processing of statistics on the carriage of goods by road
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for collecting and transmitting data on road transport by means of a goods road transport vehicle.
It aims to provide the European Commission with comparable, reliable, synchronised, regular and comprehensive statistical data on the transport of goods across the European Union (EU) by road.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all transport by road of goods between the EU countries during the 1 January to 31 December 1999 survey period.
EU countries must ensure that their methods for the collection, processing and dissemination of statistical data are designed to ensure that the statistical results transmitted pursuant to this regulation are sufficiently precise so as to enable the Commission to have at its disposal comparable data.
The data must be transmitted to Eurostat, the EU’s statistical office, on the basis of the NACE classification of goods and the classification of dangerous goods.
National authorities must forward the data to the Commission within 3 months of the end of the quarter covered by the first transmission.
Each EU country must forward a report on the methods used in compiling the data and the methods it uses to collect the data. The report must include information on:
the methods used to collect and process the data;
the type of data collected;
how the data were collected and processed
the method used to compile the data
the types of vehicles used
the number of vehicles involved
the vehicle type and the type of vehicle
the country in which the data are collected
the classification of the dangerous goods
the place of loading and unloading of goods
The Commission must transmit the results of the surveys to the European Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee and the Committee of the Regions.
Implementing acts
The implementing acts must be adopted in accordance with the examination procedure referred to in Article 9(2) of the implementing acts.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
Directive 2009/33/EC has applied since 23 February 2009 and had to become law in the EU Member States by 23 February 2012.

Summary 164:
Judicial and extrajudicial documents in civil and commercial matters — service by diplomatic or consular agents (JACs)
Judicial & extrajudicial document services in civil & commercial matters (SACS)
SACs
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EEC) No 552/2004 on the service of judicial and extrajudicial documents
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the service in the Member States of the European Union (EU) by judicial or extrajudicial agencies for the receipt and transmission of judicial or other judicial documents from another EU country.
KEY POINTS
The regulation establishes a system for the transmission and receiving of judicial & extrajudicial documents by public officers, authorities or other persons in each EU country to the European Commission.
It does not apply to:
transmitting agencies;
receiving agencies.
The European Commission is responsible for the implementation of the regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
The legislation has applied since 1 July 2004 and had to become law in the EU countries by 1 July 2005.
BACKGROUND
The EU has adopted a number of measures to improve judicial cooperation in civil matters, including:
Decision 1999/468/EC on judicial cooperation on judicial matters (see summary);
Council Decision 1999/469/EC establishing the European Judicial Cooperation Committee (EJCC) (see below);
Decisions 1999/472/EC and 1999/478/EC concerning the European Court of Justice (see consolidated version).

Summary 165:
Medicines for human use — advanced therapy medicinal products for human disease and disorders
Medical devices for human diseases and disorders — advanced therapies
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2008 on the regulation of advanced therapies for human uses
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the manufacture, marketing, labelling and supervision of advanced therapy medicines* for the treatment of diseases and dysfunctions of the human body.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to any of the following medicinal products:
a gene therapy medicinal product as defined in Part IV of Annex I to Directive 2001/83/EC (see summary),
a somatic cell therapy therapeutic product,
a tissue engineered product and
a stem cell therapy product.
It does not apply to the use of human cells, such as embryonic stem cells, or animal cells.
The European Medicines Agency (EMA) regulates the manufacture and marketing of these medicinal products.
Manufacturers must ensure that they comply with the essential requirements laid down in Directive 2003/94/EC on the principles and guidelines of good manufacturing practice in respect of medicinal products and investigational medicinal products (i.e. products that are intended to treat human diseases or disorders) and that they are in compliance with the requirements of the European Commission’s Committee for Advanced Therapies for the Development of Medicines and Biomedicine.
They must also ensure that their products are manufactured in a way that is safe and in accordance with the principles set out in Directive 2004/23/EC.
EU countries must ensure the safety and quality of the products they regulate.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
The legislation applies from 30 April 2008. EU countries had to incorporate it into national law by 30 December 2012.
BACKGROUND
  
For more information, see:
‘Advanced therapies’ (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Genetically modified human cells: stem cells are cells derived from the stem cells of a living organism.
* Somatic cells: cells or tissues derived from a human body part of the body that can be used to repair, replace, repair or replace a disease or disorder.
ACT
Commission Regulation (EU) No 550/2008 of 29 April 2008 on the Regulation of the Member States relating to the Regulation on the Medicines for Human Use (OJ L 183, 30.4.2008, pp. 1-8)

Summary 166:
Emissions of motor vehicles — type approval and type-approval requirements
Emissions from motor vehicles – type approval requirements
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2013 on type approval for motor vehicles and their trailers
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for the type approval of vehicles and trailers in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Type approval
The regulation sets out the type of vehicle for which the European Commission must grant type approval.
It also lays down the type requirements for the installation of pollution control devices (e.g. fuel injectors, exhaust systems, etc.).
Emission control devices must be installed on a vehicle in a way that reduces the effectiveness of the emission control system under conditions which may reasonably be expected to be encountered in normal vehicle operation and use.
Manufacturers are responsible for ensuring that the devices are installed correctly and that the vehicle complies with the regulation’s requirements.
The European Commission has the power to issue type approvals.
Type approvals
EU countries must ensure that type approval is granted to vehicles of a type that meets the requirements set out in the regulation.
If a vehicle does not meet the requirements for type approval, EU countries must prohibit its sale or installation.
Vehicle type approval
Vehicles that do not meet type approval must be repaired or repaired in accordance with the requirements of the regulation and its implementing measures.
National authorities must check that the vehicles are being repaired or maintained correctly and ensure that the repair and maintenance information provided by the vehicle manufacturer is accurate and up-to-date.
Regulatory requirements
The EU has to set emission limits for motor cars and trailers. These are based on the actual performance of the vehicles when in use and on the fuel consumption of the vehicle.
Fuel consumption
The fuel consumption limits are set according to the amount of fuel that a vehicle can carry out a normal driving operation.
In addition, the regulation lays down rules for in-service conformity, durability, on-board diagnostic (OBD) systems, measurement of fuel consumption and accessibility of vehicle maintenance information.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 1 July 2013.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘Emissions control devices’ on the European Agency for Safety and Health at Work website.
* KEY TERMS
* Emission control device: any element of design which senses temperature, vehicle speed, engine speed (RPM), transmission gear, manifold vacuum or any other parameter for the purpose of activating, modulating, delaying or deactivating the operation of any part of the exhaust system.
ACT

SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2004 — EU rules on the application for the authorisation of substances to be placed on the European Union (EU) market

Scope

Authorisation to place substances on EU market

Summary 168:
Accreditation, market surveillance, controls of products from non-EU countries and the CE marking (European Commission).
Accreditation*, market surveillance and controls of goods originating in other EU countries
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2004 on the accreditation of products by national authorities
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that products that are subject to European Union (EU) harmonisation legislation do not endanger health, safety or any other aspect of public interest protection.
It sets out the rules for accreditation* and market surveillance* of products.
KEY POINTS
National authorities must:
assess whether a product complies with the relevant EU legislation;
monitor accidents and harm to health which are suspected to have been caused by those products;
verify that corrective action has been taken;
follow up scientific and technical knowledge concerning safety issues.
EU countries must ensure that market surveillance authorities exercise their powers in accordance with the principle of proportionality.
National consumer protection authorities must cooperate, at national level, with national market surveillance authority and should exchange information with them relating to products which they suspect present a risk.
The European Commission must establish procedures to:
monitor complaints or reports on issues relating to risks arising in connection with products subject to EU legislation and ensure that they are promptly investigated;
check that products comply with the requirements set out in the relevant legislation and that they have been taken corrective action;
ensure that national authorities and the Commission have access to the information they need to carry out market surveillance;
establish a system for cross-border checks of products imported into the EU;
provide the European Commission with information on products that have been withdrawn or recalled from the EU market;
implement a system of peer evaluation to check whether products are complying with EU legislation.
In addition, the Commission must ensure:
that national accreditation bodies are independent and do not compete with each other;
that the Commission has access to all the relevant information it needs to ensure the proper functioning of the EU’s market surveillance system;
the Commission has the right to request national authorities to provide it with information about products that do not meet the requirements of the legislation; and
that EU countries have the power to restrict the placing on the market of a product or to require its withdrawal or recall.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The regulation has applied since 1 January 2005.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘Accreditation’ and ‘Market surveillance’ websites.

Summary 169:
Arrest warrant and extradition — mutual legal assistance between the EU and Norway and the EU countries (Arrest Warrant and Treaty on European Arrest Warrant and the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union (EU-Iceland Agreement)
AREST WARRANT AND THE TORTURE AGREEMENTS
SUMMARY OF:
Decision 2004/8/EC on the conclusion, on behalf of the EU, of the Agreement on Mutual Legal Assistance between the European Community and its Member States, the Kingdom of Norway and Iceland and the Republic of Iceland on the arrest warrant and the treaty on the extradition of persons convicted of criminal offences
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION AND OF THE AGEMENT?
The decision and the agreement aim to establish a common legal framework for the arrest and surrender by one EU country of a requested person to another EU country for the purposes of conducting a criminal prosecution or executing a custodial sentence or detention order.
The agreement aims to:
facilitate the arrest, surrender and subsequent extradition of the requested person;
ensure that the person concerned has the right to legal counsel;
promote cooperation between the authorities of the issuing and executing countries.
KEY POINTS
Scope of the agreement
The EU-Norway and Iceland agreement covers:
the arrest warrant;
the treaty on European arrest warrant (see summary);
the extradition of a person convicted of a criminal offence to another country for prosecution or for the execution of a detention order;
a number of other legal instruments, such as extradition, extradition and extradition.
It does not only apply to criminal offences, but also to non-criminal offences such as fraud, forgery, counterfeiting, money laundering and forgery.
Scope
It applies to all offences for which an EU country has issued an arrest warrant or an extradition warrant. It does not apply to the following the death of an EU citizen.
Arrest and surrender procedures
An EU country’s executing judicial authority may refuse to execute an EU arrest warrant if:
it considers that the offence for which the warrant has been issued constitutes an offence under the law of the executing country;
it does not consider the offence to be serious enough to warrant the arrest or surrender of the person; or
it has not taken a final decision on the warrant.
If the country which has issued the warrant does not take a decision on whether to execute the warrant, it must ensure that the material conditions necessary for effective surrender are fulfilled.
Surrender or subsequent extradition
The person concerned must give his/her consent before the competent judicial authorities of that country. The person must be informed of the reasons for refusing to do so and of the consequences of the refusal.
In the event of multiple requests for the same person, the decision as to which of the arrest warrants shall be executed shall be taken by the executing judicial authorities.
A person who has not given his or her consent must be handed over to the country where the warrant was issued for the purpose of prosecution or execution. The country which surrendered the person must inform the other EU countries of the reason for the refusal and the conditions for granting the person's consent.
Procedure
The executing country must inform each other of their competent authorities when it receives a request for the person to surrender or to return him/her.
Each EU country must take the necessary measures to ensure that consent and, where appropriate, renunciation, are established in such a way as to show that the persons concerned has expressed them voluntarily and in full awareness of their rights.
When a person is refused to surrender, he/she may be held in custody for up to 30 days. If the time limits are extended by a further 30 days, the person may be released.
EU countries may continue to apply bilateral or multilateral agreements or return the property without charge to the executing EU country as soon as the criminal proceedings have been terminated.
FROM WHEN DO THE DECISIONS ENTER INTO FORCE?
Decisions 2004/884/EC and 2004/9/EC entered into force on 1 July 2004.
DecISION 2004/18/EC has applied since 1 January 2005.
Amending Decision 2004/10/EC was adopted by the European Parliament and the Council on 1 January 2006.
BACKGROUND
For more information, see:
‘Arrest warrants and extradition’ on the European Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENTS
Council Decision 2004 / 8/EC of 20 June 2004 on the signature, on the behalf of Norway, of an Agreement on mutual legal aid between the Union and its member States, of its Kingdom, Norway, Iceland, the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland and the European Economic and Social Committee (EEC) (OJ L 183, 29.6.2004, pp. 1-2)
Council decision 2004/4/EC, on a number of issues related to the conclusion of an agreement between the Council and the Union countries, of



Summary 170:
Railway passengers’ rights — compensation for damage caused by a railway accident
Railways passengers‘ rights for damage to their rail cars
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2007 on compensation for damages caused by railway accidents
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rights of passengers who have been injured or killed by a rail accident on the European Union (EU) railway network.
It aims to ensure that passengers are compensated for the damage they have suffered.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to the carriage of passengers on the EU’s railway network and to the management of the railway infrastructure.
The legislation does not apply to:
travel information and reservation systems (i.e. ticket offices or selling machines);
ticket offices or ticketing machines;
railway ticketing and ticketing systems;
traffic management systems.
Railway undertakings must ensure that:
passengers have the right to be treated fairly and with due regard to their safety and health;
the right to have their ticket price reimbursed;
they are entitled to a refund of the carriage charge and to mobility assistance free of charge on board a train and during boarding and disembarking from a train.
If a passenger is killed or injured on the railway network, the railway undertaking must pay compensation to the natural person who is responsible for the death or injury. The amount of damages to be awarded must be determined in accordance with national law.
Compensation
The compensation must be paid within 15 days after the death of a natural person and not later than 15 days from the date of death.
Annex I to the compensation is set out in Annex II to the regulation.
In addition, the compensation may be waived if:
the natural person is a national of an EU country or a resident of a non-EU country;
an undertaking using the same railway infrastructure is not considered as a party to the accident;
a passenger who has been injured is not entitled to compensation for the loss of his or her right to compensation.
Exclusions of waiver and stipulation of limits
The European Commission must submit to the European Parliament and the Council a report on the setting of a minimum amount of insurance for railway undertakings by 3 December 2010.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
Directive 2007/52/EC has applied since 3 December 2007 and had to become law in the EU countries by 3 January 2008.
Amending act(s)
Regulatory (EU, Euratom) 2017/852 amends Regulation (EC), Euratom has to apply from 3 December 2017.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘Passenger rights’ on the website of the European Commission.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Commission Regulation (EEC) no 550/2007 of 25 November 2007 concerning compensation for losses caused by rail accidents
Successive amendments and corrections to Regulation 2007/54/EC have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Statistics in education and long-term care (E & T)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 852/2005 on the production of Community statistics in the fields of Education and Long-Term Care
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a common framework for the systematic production of EU statistics on the quality, scope and reliability of European education and training systems.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all European Union (EU) Member States.
It does not apply to:
the European Commission (Eurostat);
the Member States’ statistical institutes;
the EU countries’ national statistics offices;
other bodies responsible for statistics.
The scope of the regulation is set out in the annex to the regulation.
Data sources and sample size

EU Member States must provide Eurostat with data on:
education and training system characteristics;
quality of education systems and their correspondence with international classifications;
measures to improve the quality of education;
effects of education on health and well-being;
benefits of education, not covered by domains 1 and 2.
Quality of data
Data must be collected every 5 years.
National statistics offices must ensure that the data collected are up-to-date and that they respect the protection of personal data.
Monitoring
The European Commission must monitor the quality and quantity of data collected by the Member States and report to the European Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee and the Committee on the Functioning of the European Union.

Summary 173:
Accessibility and information for disabled persons and persons with reduced mobility on the bus and coach
Assessment of the accessibility and information requirements for the carriage of passengers by bus and coaches
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 864/2007 on the rights of passengers on the transport of persons with disabilities on the public transport system
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that passengers travelling by public transport in the European Union (EU) have the same rights as the general public.
It lays down minimum rights for passengers who are disabled or have reduced mobility.
KEY POINTS
Passengers have the right to:
be transported by a bus or coach within the EU;
be provided with information regarding the service before and during the journey;
have access to a connecting service if the service is cancelled or delayed.
The regulation sets out the minimum rights that passengers have to be granted by the carrier or the terminal managing body.
These rights include:
the right to transport within the territory of an EU country, irrespective of the place of establishment of the carriers, or ticket vendors;
access to the boarding point or alighting point of the service;
right to be assisted by a person in a wheelchair or other mobility device;
rights to have their luggage checked before boarding the service.
Carriers must ensure that:
passengers have access to the information they need to make a reservation;
the information is provided in a language that can be understood by all passengers;
there is assistance for disabled passengers and persons who have limited mobility;
information is provided on the availability of wheelchair-accessible buses and coaches;
transport information is available on the website of the European Commission’s Directorate-General for the Internal Market and the Single European Market.
Directive 2014/33/EU, which aims to improve the accessibility of public transport services in the EU, amends the regulation to include the right of disabled persons to travel by bus or coaches within the European Economic Area (EEA).
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?

  дабанна городна is the name of the EU country where the regulation applies.

Summary 174:
Statistics on aquaculture activities in freshwater and saltwater — EU countries’ responsibilities and methods
Statistics on aquatic species
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 852/2008 on the collection and management of statistics by EU countries on the activities conducted in freshwater* and saltwaters
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the obligations of EU countries to submit to the European Commission statistics on all the aquaulture activities conducted on their territory.
KEY POINTS
EU countries are responsible for collecting and managing the statistics on the aquatic species they undertake for the purposes of the Common Fisheries Policy (CFSP).
The statistics covered by the regulation are based on surveys or other statistically validated methods covering at least 90 % of the total production by volume or by number for the production of hatcheries and nurseries, without prejudice to the definition of ‘aquaculture’ in Article 4.
The EU countries must submit the statistics to the Commission by 31 December 2011 and every 3 years thereafter. The format in which statistics are submitted must be adopted in accordance with the management procedure laid down in Article 10(2) of Decision 1999/468/EC (see summary).
Each EU country must submit a report to the EU Parliament and to the Council on the statistics it has collected and the methods used to compile them.
By 31 December 2013, the Commission will submit an evaluation report on the data it has received.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLYORKERIES AND NURNERS
The regulation applies from 1 January 2009.
It repeals Regulation (EC, EC) No 1282/2004/2004.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission is responsible for the collection, management and dissemination of EU fisheries statistics. It is assisted by the Standing Committee for Agricultural Statistics set up by Council Decision 72/279/EEC.
For more information, see:
EU fisheries statistics (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Hatcheries & nurseries: a system of breeding and rearing of fish for the purpose of breeding or rearing fish for commercial purposes.
* Aquaculture: the practice of collecting specimens from the wild and their subsequent use in the production and sale of fish.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Commission Regulation (EU) 2016/852 of 30 November 2016 on the compilation and management by EU governments of statistics on aquatic species

Summary 175:
Convention on the Conservation and Management of Fishery Resources in the North Atlantic (Cotonou Convention) (COTM)
Convention upon the Conservation, Management and Regulation of the Fisheries in the north Atlantic of the North America and Caribbean Free Trade Association
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1224/2009 on the implementation of the convention on the conservation and management of fishery resources
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a framework for multilateral cooperation on the rational conservation of fisheries resources in the area defined by the Cotonou COTM (the North Atlantic Free Trade Area).
It sets out the rules for the inspection and surveillance of fishing vessels in this area.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all fishing vessels flying the flag of an EU country.
It does not apply to:
non-EU fishing vessels;
fishing vessels flying a flag of a non-EU country;
ships flying an international radio call-sign;
shipments of fish under the control of a fishing vessel flying a national flag.
National authorities must:
ensure that vessels carrying fish are accompanied by a special identity document to identify them;
assess the number of fishing days and the catch taken in the regulatory area since the start of fishing, or since the last catch report;
report on the quantities on-loaded and off-loaded for each transhipment of fish during the vessel’s stay in the Regulatory Area.
Inspections
Each EU country must designate an inspector to carry out inspections in its territory.
The inspector must carry out a thorough inspection under its authority. The duration of the inspection may exceed the limits laid down in the regulation.
If an inspector suspects that a vessel has committed an infringement, he/she must board and inspect the vessel. If the master consents to the boarding and inspection of the vessel, the inspection must be documented by the completion of an inspection report, as referred to in Article 20(9). Where the evidence in that report so warrants, a EU country may take such action as may be appropriate in accordance with international law.
Monitoring
The European Union (EU) Fisheries Agency (EFTA) is responsible for monitoring the activities of vessels operating in the Cotamundi area. The EFTA is assisted by the European Maritime Safety Agency (EMSA).
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
Directive 2009/12/EC has applied since 1 January 2010.
Directives 2009/13/EC and 2009/14/EU have applied since 31 December 2009.
Decision 2009/11/EU was adopted on behalf of the EU.
BACKGROUND
The COTAMOND Convention is a multilateral agreement between the European Union, the United States of America and the European Economic Area (EEA) countries.
For more information, see:
‘The North Atlantic free trade area’ on the European Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EC, EC, Euratom) No 2012/2009 of 27 December 2009 on the implementing of the Convention on the Convention of the Conservation of Fisheries in the Northern Atlantic and Caribbean Faroes (Cotamud Convention) and repealing Directives (EEC, EEA) No 552/2008 and (EEA) 2015/852 (OJ L 347, 30.12.2009, pp. 1-2)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EU, EC) No 11/2009 have been incorporated into the original document. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
RELATED DOCUMENTS

Summary 176:
Ecolabelling of agricultural products — European Union (EU) ecolabel scheme
Ecolabel of agriculture products — EU ecolabelled agricultural products
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 834/2009 on the European Union Ecolabel system
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the use of the EU’s environmental label (ecolabel) system.
It aims to promote the marketing of products bearing environmental labels at national and EU levels.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all agricultural products that fall within the scope of Regulation (EC), including:
unprocessed agricultural products;
processed foodstuffs;
seeds and vegetable oils;
sugars;
fruit and vegetables;
nutritional supplements;
nuts and seeds;
eggs;
chickpeas;
milk;
powdered milk;
coconut oil;
methane;
dairy products.
Eligibility for operators
An operator of an ecolabilised product must apply for a contract to use the EU Ecolablabel.
An EU country must notify the European Commission of its intention to award the contract to an operator.
The Commission must then draw up a standard procedure for awarding the contract.
A contract is awarded to the operator by the competent body of the country in which the contract is to be awarded. The contract must be concluded within 6 months after the Commission receives the contract and must contain the following information:
a description of the type of the operator, a description of their activities and the terms of use, a contract with the operator and the conditions for the authorisation and withdrawal of the Ecolabilabel, a list of the types of products covered by the contract
the type of product to be labelled and the type and quantity of products to be marketed under the contract;
the name of the company responsible for the certification of the product;
a statement of the quality of the products to which the label is applied.
If the Commission considers that the contract does not meet the requirements of the regulation, it must inform the operator of the reasons for its decision.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULTRY TO ENTRY INTO FORCE?
   
 
It entered into force on 1 January 2010.
BACKGROUND
  * KEY TERMS
  белодналка бодкака  гародска, баркагана карнакка and годанна  ходранка are the official names of EU countries’ national ecolablabelling systems.
* Ecolabels are used to indicate that a product has been certified by the International Organisation for Standardisation of Chemicals (ISO) as having a high environmental impact and that it is safe for human health and the environment.
For more information, see:
‘Ecolabilisation’ (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENT
 			
Commission Regulation (Euratom) No 461/2009 of 26 October 2009 on the application of the Regulation of the European Parliament and of the Council of 26 September 2009 establishing a European Union Environmental Label System (EEC) (OJ L 183, 28.10.2009, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2018/852 have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
RELATED DOCUMENTS
  —
Regulations (EU and Euratom Implementing Decision (EU), Euratom (EU).

Directive 2014/43/EU of the United Nations Environment Programme of the World Trade Organization on the protection of human health, the environment and the health of animals and plants (see consolidated version). See summary.

Summary 177:
Protection of patents on medicines — certificate of authorisation for their use in the European Union (EU) and in the United States
Protection on patents on medicinal products — certificate for their uses in the EU and the US
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 852/2008 on the protection of patents for medicinal products
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the conditions for granting a patent on a medicinal product to the holder of a pharmaceutical patent.
It codifies and repeals Regulation (Euratom) No 1901/2006.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to patents granted by the European Commission or by the EU countries’ competent industrial property offices. It does not apply to certificates granted in accordance with the national legislation of a Member State before 2 January 1993 or to applications for a certificate filed in accordance to that legislation before 2 July 1992.
The basic patent must be granted within 6 months of the date on which the patent is granted or on whose behalf it was granted and the authorisation to place the product on the market was obtained, unless the EU country designates another authority for the purpose.
An application for a patent is lodged with the competent national industrial property office of the Member State which granted the patent or on its behalf and in which the product to which it relates. The application must contain the particulars of the patent, the product and a copy of the certificate.
A certificate is granted to the patent holder or his successor in title if they have the right to use the product for the first time.
the certificate is valid for a maximum of 20 years
The certificate may be renewed for a further 20 years if the patent expires or if the term of patent exceeds 20 years.
If the certificate expires or is invalidated, the holder is entitled to a declaration of invalidity of the basic patent and to the revocation of the corresponding basic patent. The certificate may also be invalidated for a period of 10 years if it expires or lapses.
Licence of the product
Licences for the manufacture of medicines are issued by the competent authority of an EU country.
Manufacturers must apply for a licence to manufacture medicines in the country where the patent has been granted.
Lodging of an application
The applicant must lodge an application with the authority of the country which granted a patent and the authority which authorised the manufacture or placing of the medicine on the European market.
Application for a licence must be lodged within six months of:
the date of the granting of a patent or the date when the product was authorised to be manufactured or placed on the EU market
the day on which a certificate was granted or issued for the second time
the year on which an application was lodged for an extension of the duration of a certificate already granted or where an application for an additional certificate is pending.
Applying for a Licence
The application must include all the information necessary to obtain a licence, including the name and registered number of the manufacturer and the name of the labelling of the medicinal product.
Applicants must lodge the application with an authority which has the power to grant or reject a licence.
Applications for a license must contain all the necessary information, such as the name, registered number and postal address of the manufacturing or placing place of manufacture of the medical product and the number of registered numbers of the laboratory that performed the clinical trials and the laboratory where the clinical trial was carried out.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
    бакованска грашка  годна бълара вака, глачкага и горовна  ханка and ганца даннабарка (OJ L 210, 20.6.2008, pp. 1-8)
Regulations (EC, Euratom) and (EU, Euram) No 1049/2008 have applied since 1 January 2009.
BACKGROUND
 
  Баконсгка is a legal instrument that ensures that patents on pharmaceutical products, especially those that are the result of long, costly research will not continue to be developed in the Community and in Europe unless they are covered by favourable rules that provide for sufficient protection to encourage such research.
For more information, see:
‘Licences of medicinal products’ (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Patent holder: the person who holds a patent for a pharmaceutical product or the body responsible under national law for granting it.
* Authorised manufacturer: the company or body responsible for authorising the manufacture, placing on the markets or placing a medicine on sale.

Summary 178:
Civil and commercial matters — jurisdiction of the courts of the countries bound by the Convention on the jurisdiction of insurance policyholders and co-insurers (Lugano Convention on civil and commercial law)
Civil & commercial matters – jurisdiction of insurers and their subsidiaries
SUMMARY OF:
Decision (EU) 2017/852 on the conclusion of the Lugano Convention — Jurisdiction of the Courts of Justice of the Countries of the European Union (Lagano Convention)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION AND OF THE CONVENTION?
The decision approves the signing, on behalf of the EU, by the European Community (now the EU) and the European Economic Area (EEA) countries of the Treaty on European Union, of the Swiss Convention on Civil and Commercial Law (Ligano Convention).
The convention aims to ensure that the courts in the EU and the EEA countries have the same jurisdiction when dealing with insurance claims.
KEY POINTS
Scope of the convention
The Lugano convention applies to all insurance claims, including claims brought by the policyholder, the insured or a beneficiary, in the courts for the place where the insurer is domiciled.
It does not apply to claims brought in civil or commercial matters.
Insurers may be sued:
in the court of the country where they have their domicile;
in another country where the defendant has his or her place of residence; or
in a court of residence in another EU country.
Defendants may also be sued in the same way as the policyholders.
DATE OF ENDS OF ENTRY INTO FORCELEBRATION
The agreement entered into force
On 1 January 2018.
BACKGROUND
The Swiss Convention is one of a series of international treaties signed by the EU countries, including the Rome Statute of the International Court of Justice (ICJ) of the World Trade Organisation (ICTY).
It has been amended several times, most recently by Decision (EU, Euratom) 2018/853.
For more information, see:
‘The Swiss Conventions’ on the European Commission’s website.
